Miracles
beginner

The Baraka of Praying Behind a Saint
First karama story: meat remains raw after being present during prayer with Imam Sanusi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the baraka of praying behind a righteous Imam can manifest in extraordinary physical phenomena.

Core Idea
Baraka from the saint's prayer can even prevent fire from affecting matter.

This first anecdote from the life of Imam Sanusi illustrates the tangible blessing (baraka) that flows from following a saintly Imam in prayer. A man enters the mosque with raw meat and prays behind the Imam. Later, despite hours of cooking, the meat remains raw, leading the Imam to attribute it to the protection of those who pray behind him.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote
Read the story carefully, noting the sequence of events and the Imam's response.
2
Identify the miracle
What is extraordinary here? The meat does not cook despite prolonged exposure to fire. Why does the Imam interpret it as a sign?
Think about the concept of baraka (blessing) and its physical effects.
3
Understand the lesson
This story teaches that the baraka of a saint can have tangible consequences, affirming the reality of karamat.
The Imam says 'I hope that whoever prays behind me, the fire will not overcome him' – a spiritual protection with a physical sign.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن كراماته : أنَّ رجلاً اشترى لحماً من السوق، فسمع الإقامة في المسجد، فدخل واللحم معه يحمله، فخاف من طرحه فوات ركعة، وكبر على هذه الحال، فلما سلَّم وعاد إلى أهله طبخ أهله اللحم إلى صلاة العشاء فلم ينضج، فأرادوا طرحه فإذا هو على حاله بدمه، فقالوا : لعله لحم شارف، فباتوا يوقدون عليه إلى الصبح، فلم يتغيَّر عن حاله ! فتذكر الرجل، فذهب إلى الإمام فأعلمه بذلك، فقال له : يا بني؛ أرجو الله تعالى أنَّ كل من صلى ورائي لا تعدو عليه النار، ولعل هذا اللحم كان معك حين صليت معي، ولكن اكتم ذلك. ومن ذلك : أنه كان يقول ثقةً بمولاه : ( من كانت له إلى الله حاجة فليتوسل بنا وليقدمنا )، فرُوي أنَّ امرأة ضاع منها مفتاح بيتها، فحاولت بكل حيلة فتحه فلم تفلح، فتوسلت بالشيخ وبجاهه عند ربه، ففتح الباب وانحل القفل. ومن ذلك : تأليفه للشرح الكبير لـ «الحوفية »، الذي سماه : «المقرب المستوفي »، ألَّفه وهو ابن تسع عشرة سنة، فلما وقف عليه الشيخ القطب الحسن أبركان تعجب منه، وأمر بإخفائه حتى يكمل مُؤلّفه أربعين سنة؛ لئلا يصاب بالعين، ويقول له : لا نظير له فيما أعلم، ودعا لمؤلفه. ومن ذلك : أنه رئي يوماً كثير الانقباض متغير اللون، فسئل عن ذلك، فأجاب بعد إلحاح وشرط كتم الأمر، فقال : أطلعني الله تعالى على رؤية جهنم وما فيها، نعوذ بالله منها، فمن حينئذ صرت أتغير وأحزن إلى الآن، فهذا سبب تغيري.
And among his karamat (miracles of saints): that a man bought meat from the market, and heard the iqama in the mosque, so he entered while the meat was with him, carrying it, and he feared that if he threw it he would miss a rak'a, so he said the takbir in this state. When he had finished the prayer and returned to his family, his family cooked the meat until the evening prayer ['isha'] but it did not cook. They wanted to throw it away, but it was as it was, with its blood. They said: Perhaps it is meat of an old camel. So they kept kindling a fire under it until morning, but it did not change from its state. Then the man remembered, so he went to the Imam and informed him of that. He said to him: O my son, I hope from Allah Almighty that whoever prays behind me, the fire will not overcome him. Perhaps this meat was with you when you prayed with me, but keep that secret. And among that: that he used to say, trusting in his Lord: 'Whoever has a need from Allah, let him seek intercession through us [tawassul] and put us forward.' It is narrated that a woman lost the key to her house, and she tried every trick to open it but did not succeed. So she sought intercession through the Shaykh and his standing with his Lord, and the door opened and the lock came undone. And among that: his authorship of the great commentary on 'al-Hawfiyya', which he named 'al-Muqrib al-Mustawfi'. He wrote it when he was nineteen years old. When the Shaykh al-Qutb al-Hasan Abrkan saw it, he marveled at it, and ordered it to be hidden until its author completed forty years, lest he be struck by the evil eye, and he said to him: There is no equal to it as far as I know, and he prayed for its author. And among that: that he was seen one day very depressed, his color changed. He was asked about that, and he answered after insistence and the condition of keeping the matter secret. He said: Allah Almighty showed me the vision of Hell and what is in it – we seek refuge with Allah from it. From that time I became changed and sad until now, and this is the reason for my change.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a collection of four karama stories from the life of Imam Sanusi, narrated by his biographer. The first story illustrates the blessing (baraka) of praying behind the Imam: a man brought raw meat into prayer, and despite cooking all evening and night, it remained raw and unchanged – the Imam links this to the protection from fire for those who pray behind him. The second story shows the efficacy of tawassul (seeking intercession through the saint): a woman unable to open her lock invokes the Imam and the lock opens. The third emphasizes the Imam's precocious knowledge and the protection from envy: his great commentary written at age 19 was ordered hidden until 40 by a saint who praised it. The fourth is a warning: the Imam saw a vision of Hell, and that experience left him permanently changed and sorrowful. All four anecdotes serve to confirm the reality and varied forms of karamat as accepted by Ahl al-Sunna.

Key Terms
كرامات
بركة
الإمام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Karama stories are mere folklore without theological significance.
Correction: In Ahl al-Sunna, karamat are real and serve as proofs of the saint's rank and the truth of Islam.

Checkpoint
According to the story, why did the meat not cook despite being on fire all night?
A) Because it was from an old camel
B) Because of the baraka of praying behind Imam Sanusi
C) Because the fire was not hot enough
D) Because the man had made a vow

Key Takeaway
The baraka of a saintly Imam can manifest as physical preservation, demonstrating the reality of karamat.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you knew that a certain imam's baraka could protect you from harm, would you go out of your way to pray behind him? What does your answer reveal about how much you value the spiritual quality of those you follow in worship?
?
The man feared missing a rak'a more than the inconvenience of carrying meat. When you are in a hurry, do you still prioritize the prayer and its proper performance over your worldly tasks? Are you willing to make small sacrifices for the sake of not losing the reward of the congregation?
?
The imam expressed hope that those who pray behind him are saved from the fire. Do you place your trust in such promises from righteous people, or do you rely solely on your own deeds? How does this story challenge you to seek out and respect the saints among you?

The Efficacy of Tawassul Through the Saint
Second karama story: woman's lock opens through tawassul to Imam Sanusi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the practice of tawassul (seeking intercession) through the saints and how it can be answered.

Core Idea
Tawassul through the saint can lead to the opening of physical and spiritual locks.

The second anecdote highlights the practice of tawassul – seeking intercession through the saint. Imam Sanusi himself encouraged people to seek Allah's help through him. A woman who lost her key tried every method but failed, then she sought intercession through the Imam, and the lock opened.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote
Read the story and note the Imam's direct quote about tawassul.
2
Identify the tawassul
Notice how the woman sought intercession through the Imam's rank with Allah. This is tawassul.
Tawassul is a legitimate practice in Sunni Islam.
3
Reflect on the lesson
This story affirms that tawassul is effective and that saints are a means of blessing.
Consider the theological implications of seeking intercession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن كراماته : أنَّ رجلاً اشترى لحماً من السوق، فسمع الإقامة في المسجد، فدخل واللحم معه يحمله، فخاف من طرحه فوات ركعة، وكبر على هذه الحال، فلما سلَّم وعاد إلى أهله طبخ أهله اللحم إلى صلاة العشاء فلم ينضج، فأرادوا طرحه فإذا هو على حاله بدمه، فقالوا : لعله لحم شارف، فباتوا يوقدون عليه إلى الصبح، فلم يتغيَّر عن حاله ! فتذكر الرجل، فذهب إلى الإمام فأعلمه بذلك، فقال له : يا بني؛ أرجو الله تعالى أنَّ كل من صلى ورائي لا تعدو عليه النار، ولعل هذا اللحم كان معك حين صليت معي، ولكن اكتم ذلك. ومن ذلك : أنه كان يقول ثقةً بمولاه : ( من كانت له إلى الله حاجة فليتوسل بنا وليقدمنا )، فرُوي أنَّ امرأة ضاع منها مفتاح بيتها، فحاولت بكل حيلة فتحه فلم تفلح، فتوسلت بالشيخ وبجاهه عند ربه، ففتح الباب وانحل القفل. ومن ذلك : تأليفه للشرح الكبير لـ «الحوفية »، الذي سماه : «المقرب المستوفي »، ألَّفه وهو ابن تسع عشرة سنة، فلما وقف عليه الشيخ القطب الحسن أبركان تعجب منه، وأمر بإخفائه حتى يكمل مُؤلّفه أربعين سنة؛ لئلا يصاب بالعين، ويقول له : لا نظير له فيما أعلم، ودعا لمؤلفه. ومن ذلك : أنه رئي يوماً كثير الانقباض متغير اللون، فسئل عن ذلك، فأجاب بعد إلحاح وشرط كتم الأمر، فقال : أطلعني الله تعالى على رؤية جهنم وما فيها، نعوذ بالله منها، فمن حينئذ صرت أتغير وأحزن إلى الآن، فهذا سبب تغيري.
And among his karamat (miracles of saints): that a man bought meat from the market, and heard the iqama in the mosque, so he entered while the meat was with him, carrying it, and he feared that if he threw it he would miss a rak'a, so he said the takbir in this state. When he had finished the prayer and returned to his family, his family cooked the meat until the evening prayer ['isha'] but it did not cook. They wanted to throw it away, but it was as it was, with its blood. They said: Perhaps it is meat of an old camel. So they kept kindling a fire under it until morning, but it did not change from its state. Then the man remembered, so he went to the Imam and informed him of that. He said to him: O my son, I hope from Allah Almighty that whoever prays behind me, the fire will not overcome him. Perhaps this meat was with you when you prayed with me, but keep that secret. And among that: that he used to say, trusting in his Lord: 'Whoever has a need from Allah, let him seek intercession through us [tawassul] and put us forward.' It is narrated that a woman lost the key to her house, and she tried every trick to open it but did not succeed. So she sought intercession through the Shaykh and his standing with his Lord, and the door opened and the lock came undone. And among that: his authorship of the great commentary on 'al-Hawfiyya', which he named 'al-Muqrib al-Mustawfi'. He wrote it when he was nineteen years old. When the Shaykh al-Qutb al-Hasan Abrkan saw it, he marveled at it, and ordered it to be hidden until its author completed forty years, lest he be struck by the evil eye, and he said to him: There is no equal to it as far as I know, and he prayed for its author. And among that: that he was seen one day very depressed, his color changed. He was asked about that, and he answered after insistence and the condition of keeping the matter secret. He said: Allah Almighty showed me the vision of Hell and what is in it – we seek refuge with Allah from it. From that time I became changed and sad until now, and this is the reason for my change.

Commentary
This passage is a collection of four karama stories from the life of Imam Sanusi, narrated by his biographer. The first story illustrates the blessing (baraka) of praying behind the Imam: a man brought raw meat into prayer, and despite cooking all evening and night, it remained raw and unchanged – the Imam links this to the protection from fire for those who pray behind him. The second story shows the efficacy of tawassul (seeking intercession through the saint): a woman unable to open her lock invokes the Imam and the lock opens. The third emphasizes the Imam's precocious knowledge and the protection from envy: his great commentary written at age 19 was ordered hidden until 40 by a saint who praised it. The fourth is a warning: the Imam saw a vision of Hell, and that experience left him permanently changed and sorrowful. All four anecdotes serve to confirm the reality and varied forms of karamat as accepted by Ahl al-Sunna.

Key Terms
توسل
كرامات
الشيخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Tawassul is shirk because it involves asking a created being for help.
Correction: In Ahl al-Sunna, tawassul is seeking Allah through the rank of a saint, which is permissible and encouraged.

Checkpoint
What did Imam Sanusi say about those who have a need from Allah?
A) They should make du'a directly
B) They should seek intercession through him
C) They should give charity
D) They should pray at night

Key Takeaway
Tawassul through the saints is a valid means of supplication, as shown by this karama.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a problem that seems impossible to solve, what is your first reaction—do you immediately turn to tawassul, or do you exhaust every worldly trick first? What does your habit reveal about your trust in the means of the saints? Will you commit to making tawassul your first resort from today?
?
The woman lost her key—literally unable to enter her own home. What 'key' have you lost in your life: a relationship, a livelihood, a skill, or perhaps your connection to Allah? Are you willing to seek tawassul with that specific need right now, naming a righteous person and asking through their rank?
?
Imam Sanusi said 'whoever has a need... let him seek intercession through us'. This offer includes you. What need is so deep that you have not dared to bring it to Allah via tawassul? Write it down now and recite the Imam's phrase 'فليتوسل بنا' as you make du'a. What stops you from doing this daily?

Protecting Knowledge from the Evil Eye
Third karama story: Imam Sanusi's commentary written at 19, hidden until 40 to avoid evil eye.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the importance of protecting exceptional knowledge from envy through the story of Imam Sanusi's early commentary.

Core Idea
Precocious knowledge requires protection from the evil eye.

The third anecdote reveals Imam Sanusi's exceptional scholarship: he authored a major commentary at age 19. A saintly figure, Shaykh al-Hasan Abrkan, ordered the work hidden until the author turned 40 to protect him from the evil eye, showing the reality of envy.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote
Read the story and note the age at which the commentary was written and the instruction given.
2
Identify the precaution
Why did the Shaykh order the work hidden? Consider the concept of 'ayn (evil eye).
The evil eye is real and can harm those who are envied.
3
Understand the lesson
This story teaches that knowledge is a blessing that should be protected from envy.
It also shows the recognition of Imam Sanusi's greatness by another saint.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن كراماته : أنَّ رجلاً اشترى لحماً من السوق، فسمع الإقامة في المسجد، فدخل واللحم معه يحمله، فخاف من طرحه فوات ركعة، وكبر على هذه الحال، فلما سلَّم وعاد إلى أهله طبخ أهله اللحم إلى صلاة العشاء فلم ينضج، فأرادوا طرحه فإذا هو على حاله بدمه، فقالوا : لعله لحم شارف، فباتوا يوقدون عليه إلى الصبح، فلم يتغيَّر عن حاله ! فتذكر الرجل، فذهب إلى الإمام فأعلمه بذلك، فقال له : يا بني؛ أرجو الله تعالى أنَّ كل من صلى ورائي لا تعدو عليه النار، ولعل هذا اللحم كان معك حين صليت معي، ولكن اكتم ذلك. ومن ذلك : أنه كان يقول ثقةً بمولاه : ( من كانت له إلى الله حاجة فليتوسل بنا وليقدمنا )، فرُوي أنَّ امرأة ضاع منها مفتاح بيتها، فحاولت بكل حيلة فتحه فلم تفلح، فتوسلت بالشيخ وبجاهه عند ربه، ففتح الباب وانحل القفل. ومن ذلك : تأليفه للشرح الكبير لـ «الحوفية »، الذي سماه : «المقرب المستوفي »، ألَّفه وهو ابن تسع عشرة سنة، فلما وقف عليه الشيخ القطب الحسن أبركان تعجب منه، وأمر بإخفائه حتى يكمل مُؤلّفه أربعين سنة؛ لئلا يصاب بالعين، ويقول له : لا نظير له فيما أعلم، ودعا لمؤلفه. ومن ذلك : أنه رئي يوماً كثير الانقباض متغير اللون، فسئل عن ذلك، فأجاب بعد إلحاح وشرط كتم الأمر، فقال : أطلعني الله تعالى على رؤية جهنم وما فيها، نعوذ بالله منها، فمن حينئذ صرت أتغير وأحزن إلى الآن، فهذا سبب تغيري.
And among his karamat (miracles of saints): that a man bought meat from the market, and heard the iqama in the mosque, so he entered while the meat was with him, carrying it, and he feared that if he threw it he would miss a rak'a, so he said the takbir in this state. When he had finished the prayer and returned to his family, his family cooked the meat until the evening prayer ['isha'] but it did not cook. They wanted to throw it away, but it was as it was, with its blood. They said: Perhaps it is meat of an old camel. So they kept kindling a fire under it until morning, but it did not change from its state. Then the man remembered, so he went to the Imam and informed him of that. He said to him: O my son, I hope from Allah Almighty that whoever prays behind me, the fire will not overcome him. Perhaps this meat was with you when you prayed with me, but keep that secret. And among that: that he used to say, trusting in his Lord: 'Whoever has a need from Allah, let him seek intercession through us [tawassul] and put us forward.' It is narrated that a woman lost the key to her house, and she tried every trick to open it but did not succeed. So she sought intercession through the Shaykh and his standing with his Lord, and the door opened and the lock came undone. And among that: his authorship of the great commentary on 'al-Hawfiyya', which he named 'al-Muqrib al-Mustawfi'. He wrote it when he was nineteen years old. When the Shaykh al-Qutb al-Hasan Abrkan saw it, he marveled at it, and ordered it to be hidden until its author completed forty years, lest he be struck by the evil eye, and he said to him: There is no equal to it as far as I know, and he prayed for its author. And among that: that he was seen one day very depressed, his color changed. He was asked about that, and he answered after insistence and the condition of keeping the matter secret. He said: Allah Almighty showed me the vision of Hell and what is in it – we seek refuge with Allah from it. From that time I became changed and sad until now, and this is the reason for my change.

Commentary
This passage is a collection of four karama stories from the life of Imam Sanusi, narrated by his biographer. The first story illustrates the blessing (baraka) of praying behind the Imam: a man brought raw meat into prayer, and despite cooking all evening and night, it remained raw and unchanged – the Imam links this to the protection from fire for those who pray behind him. The third emphasizes the Imam's precocious knowledge and the protection from envy: his great commentary written at age 19 was ordered hidden until 40 by a saint who praised it. The fourth is a warning: the Imam saw a vision of Hell, and that experience left him permanently changed and sorrowful. All four anecdotes serve to confirm the reality and varied forms of karamat as accepted by Ahl al-Sunna.

Key Terms
شرح
عين
كرامات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The evil eye is superstition and has no basis in Islam.
Correction: The evil eye is recognized in Islamic tradition, and this story shows that even saints take precautions against it.

Checkpoint
How old was Imam Sanusi when he wrote the commentary, and until what age was it ordered hidden?
A) 19, hidden until 30
B) 19, hidden until 40
C) 25, hidden until 40
D) 19, hidden until 50

Key Takeaway
Exceptional gifts, especially in knowledge, should be protected from envy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is there any gift or knowledge Allah has given you that you are showing off or failing to protect? How can you take a step today to shield it from envy?
?
When someone praises you, do you feel proud or do you immediately seek protection from the evil eye? What does your reaction reveal about your reliance on Allah?
?
The shaykh ordered hiding the work not out of shame but out of wisdom. Is there a part of your life—your worship, your learning, your talents—that you need to guard more carefully from the eyes of others? What will you do about it this week?

The Vision of Hell and Its Effect on the Saint
Fourth karama story: Imam Sanusi's vision of Hell and its lasting effect on him.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a saint's vision of the afterlife can transform their spiritual state.

Core Idea
A vision of Hell can forever change a saint's disposition.

The final anecdote describes a profound spiritual experience: Imam Sanusi was granted a vision of Hell, which left him permanently sorrowful and changed. This demonstrates the reality of such visions and their impact on the saints.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote
Read the story, noting the saint's outward change and the reason he gives.
2
Identify the vision
What did the Imam see? How did it affect him?
This is a karama of inner unveiling (kashf).
3
Reflect on the lesson
This story teaches that awareness of the Hereafter can deeply influence a saint's life.
It also shows the reality of Hell and the sincerity of the saints.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن كراماته : أنَّ رجلاً اشترى لحماً من السوق، فسمع الإقامة في المسجد، فدخل واللحم معه يحمله، فخاف من طرحه فوات ركعة، وكبر على هذه الحال، فلما سلَّم وعاد إلى أهله طبخ أهله اللحم إلى صلاة العشاء فلم ينضج، فأرادوا طرحه فإذا هو على حاله بدمه، فقالوا : لعله لحم شارف، فباتوا يوقدون عليه إلى الصبح، فلم يتغيَّر عن حاله ! فتذكر الرجل، فذهب إلى الإمام فأعلمه بذلك، فقال له : يا بني؛ أرجو الله تعالى أنَّ كل من صلى ورائي لا تعدو عليه النار، ولعل هذا اللحم كان معك حين صليت معي، ولكن اكتم ذلك. ومن ذلك : أنه كان يقول ثقةً بمولاه : ( من كانت له إلى الله حاجة فليتوسل بنا وليقدمنا )، فرُوي أنَّ امرأة ضاع منها مفتاح بيتها، فحاولت بكل حيلة فتحه فلم تفلح، فتوسلت بالشيخ وبجاهه عند ربه، ففتح الباب وانحل القفل. ومن ذلك : تأليفه للشرح الكبير لـ «الحوفية »، الذي سماه : «المقرب المستوفي »، ألَّفه وهو ابن تسع عشرة سنة، فلما وقف عليه الشيخ القطب الحسن أبركان تعجب منه، وأمر بإخفائه حتى يكمل مُؤلّفه أربعين سنة؛ لئلا يصاب بالعين، ويقول له : لا نظير له فيما أعلم، ودعا لمؤلفه. ومن ذلك : أنه رئي يوماً كثير الانقباض متغير اللون، فسئل عن ذلك، فأجاب بعد إلحاح وشرط كتم الأمر، فقال : أطلعني الله تعالى على رؤية جهنم وما فيها، نعوذ بالله منها، فمن حينئذ صرت أتغير وأحزن إلى الآن، فهذا سبب تغيري.
And among his karamat (miracles of saints): that a man bought meat from the market, and heard the iqama in the mosque, so he entered while the meat was with him, carrying it, and he feared that if he threw it he would miss a rak'a, so he said the takbir in this state. When he had finished the prayer and returned to his family, his family cooked the meat until the evening prayer ['isha'] but it did not cook. They wanted to throw it away, but it was as it was, with its blood. They said: Perhaps it is meat of an old camel. So they kept kindling a fire under it until morning, but it did not change from its state. Then the man remembered, so he went to the Imam and informed him of that. He said to him: O my son, I hope from Allah Almighty that whoever prays behind me, the fire will not overcome him. Perhaps this meat was with you when you prayed with me, but keep that secret. And among that: that he used to say, trusting in his Lord: 'Whoever has a need from Allah, let him seek intercession through us [tawassul] and put us forward.' It is narrated that a woman lost the key to her house, and she tried every trick to open it but did not succeed. So she sought intercession through the Shaykh and his standing with his Lord, and the door opened and the lock came undone. And among that: his authorship of the great commentary on 'al-Hawfiyya', which he named 'al-Muqrib al-Mustawfi'. He wrote it when he was nineteen years old. When the Shaykh al-Qutb al-Hasan Abrkan saw it, he marveled at it, and ordered it to be hidden until its author completed forty years, lest he be struck by the evil eye, and he said to him: There is no equal to it as far as I know, and he prayed for its author. And among that: that he was seen one day very depressed, his color changed. He was asked about that, and he answered after insistence and the condition of keeping the matter secret. He said: Allah Almighty showed me the vision of Hell and what is in it – we seek refuge with Allah from it. From that time I became changed and sad until now, and this is the reason for my change.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a collection of four karama stories from the life of Imam Sanusi, narrated by his biographer. The first story illustrates the blessing (baraka) of praying behind the Imam: a man brought raw meat into prayer, and despite cooking all evening and night, it remained raw and unchanged – the Imam links this to the protection from fire for those who pray behind him. The second story shows the efficacy of tawassul (seeking intercession through the saint): a woman unable to open her lock invokes the Imam and the lock opens. The third emphasizes the Imam's precocious knowledge and the protection from envy: his great commentary written at age 19 was ordered hidden until 40 by a saint who praised it. The fourth is a warning: the Imam saw a vision of Hell, and that experience left him permanently changed and sorrowful. All four anecdotes serve to confirm the reality and varied forms of karamat as accepted by Ahl al-Sunna.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Saints are immune to fear or sadness.
Correction: Saints can experience profound emotions, especially when confronted with the realities of the Hereafter.

Checkpoint

A) Due to a personal loss

C) Because of his old age
D) Because of a dream

Key Takeaway
Visions of the Hereafter are real and can profoundly impact a saint's life.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imagine being shown the reality of Hell as Imam Sanusi was. Would you be willing to be changed forever, or do you prefer to remain comfortable in your current state? What is one small change you can make today to live with more awareness of the Hereafter?
?
The saint insisted on secrecy. Do you seek recognition for your spiritual efforts, or are you content with Allah knowing? When was the last time you hid a good deed?
?
If you truly believed that your every action is weighed for the Hereafter, what would you stop doing immediately? Write one specific action you will stop today because of this lesson.

Sanusi on the Reality of Karamat and Refutation of Deniers
Imam Sanusi states his doctrine on karamat and criticizes both deniers and extremists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Sanusi's balanced doctrine on karamat, including their high status, the error of denying them, and the danger of extremism among some Sunnis.

Core Idea
Karamat are real, almost like miracles, but denying them or declaring takfir over them are both wrong.

In this passage, Imam Sanusi presents the mainstream Sunni view on the miracles of saints (karamat). He draws a clear line between accepting karamat and falling into extremism. His words provide a model of balanced theology that respects divine power while avoiding reckless condemnation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic source and its English translation carefully. Notice the flow from doctrinal statement to quote to criticism.
The passage includes a direct quote from Sanusi's own commentary.
2
Identify Sanusi's main claim
Sanusi states that karamat almost join prophetic miracles in their manifestation. This is a strong affirmation of their reality and significance.
3
Understand the two types of error
First, innovators deny karamat because they have never experienced them. Second, some Sunni jurists overreact by declaring disbelief on those who accept certain karamat, like the story of Ibrahim ibn Adham.
Sanusi finds the second error more surprising.
4
Reflect on the balanced position
Sanusi neither limits God's power nor allows reckless takfir. This middle path is characteristic of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a.
Consider how this balanced approach applies to other theological issues.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومذهب الإمام السنوسي في الكرامة ووقوعها مذهب عامة المحققين من أهل السنة والجماعة، وقد نثر الحديث عنها مختصراً تارة ومطولاً أخرى في سنوسياته المباركة، وله عبارة ذهبية نقدية لم تحجم قدرة الله تعالى ولم تقصر من شأن الكرامة في « شرح العقيدة الوسطى » إذ قال فيها : ( فكرامات الأولياء باعتبار ظهورها تكاد تلحق بمعجزات الأنبياء وإنكارها ليس بعجيب من أهل البدع والأهواء؛ إذ لم يشاهدوا ذلك من أنفسهم قطّ ( إلى أن قال : ( وإنما العجب من بعض فقهاء أهل السنة؛ حيث قال فيما روي عن إبراهيم بن أدهم أنهم رأوه بالبصرة يوم التروية وفي ذلك اليوم بمكة : إنَّ من اعتقد جواز ذلك يكفر !! ).
And the doctrine of Imam Sanusi concerning karamat (miracles of saints) and their occurrence is the doctrine of the generality of verifiers (muhaqqiqun) from Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a. He has scattered discourse about it, sometimes briefly and sometimes at length, in his blessed Sanusiyyat. And he has a golden, critical statement that neither limits the power of Allah Almighty nor diminishes the status of karamat, in 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta', where he said: 'Indeed, the karamat of the saints, in terms of their manifestation, almost join the miracles of the prophets (mu'jizat al-anbiya'). Denying them is not strange from the people of innovation (bid'a) and desires (ahwa'), since they have never witnessed that from themselves at all.' Then he said: 'Rather, the wonder is from some jurists of Ahl al-Sunna, regarding what is narrated about Ibrahim ibn Adham that they saw him in Basra on the day of Tarwiya and on that same day in Mecca. They said: Whoever considers that permissible is a disbeliever (kafir)!'
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage states the author's position on the doctrine of karamat. It identifies Imam Sanusi's view as that of the majority of verified scholars from Ahl al-Sunna. Then it introduces a quote from his own work 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta' as a model statement that properly balances divine power and the reality of karamat. In the quote, Sanusi first establishes that karamat are so striking that they almost match prophetic miracles (mu'jizat) in their visibility. He then explains that denial of karamat is expected from people of innovation (bid'a) who have never experienced them themselves. Finally, he expresses wonder at some Sunni jurists who go too far by declaring disbelief (takfir) upon those who believe in certain karamat – specifically the story of Ibrahim ibn Adham being in two places at once (Basra and Mecca on the same day). Thus, the passage affirms the reality of karamat, criticizes both the innovators who deny them and the extremists among Sunnis who over-react, and upholds the balanced Sunni position.

Misconception: Karamat are exactly the same as prophetic miracles.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that karamat 'almost join' but are not identical; they are close in manifestation but distinct in nature.

Checkpoint

Imam Sanusi affirms the reality of karamat, warns against denying them, and condemns excessive takfir by some Sunnis.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Sanusi is astonished at those who declare takfir over a saint's miracle. Have you ever been quick to label someone as deviant or misguided because of a belief that you personally find hard to accept? The passage says denial from innovators is 'not strange' because they never witnessed such things. Will you start today by praying for openness to His wonders?

Definition of Miracle and Its First Condition: Act of Allah
Sanusi defines miracle and explains the first condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of a miracle according to Sanusi and the meaning of its first condition that it is an act of Allah.

Core Idea
A miracle is a divine act that proves prophethood.

Sanusi begins his discussion of miracles by giving a precise definition and then explaining each condition. The first condition—that a miracle is an act of Allah—distinguishes it from eternal things and clarifies that even the prophet's recitation is a miracle for him alone. In this lesson, we explore this condition in detail.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition and first condition
Read the Arabic text of the definition and the first condition carefully. Notice how Sanusi uses the term 'act of Allah' to exclude the eternal.
The term 'qadīm' here means 'eternal' (uncreated).
2
Understand the two types of acts included
The passage divides acts into those involving originated power (like recitation) and those not (like reviving the dead). Understand why both are valid miracles.
Some scholars argue that miracles must be of the second type.
3
Reflect on the distinction
Ask yourself why the prophet's recitation is a miracle for him but not for others. This shows that miracles are specific to the prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتفضَّلَ سبحانَهُ بتأييدهم بالمعجزة الدالة على صدقهم ؛ وهي فعلُ الله سبحانه ، خارق للعادة ، مُقارِنُ لدعوى الرسالة ، مُتحدّى بهِ قبل وقوعِهِ ، غيرُ مُكَذِّبِ يُعجِزُ مَنْ يبغي معارضته عن الإتيان بمثلِهِ

فاحترزَ بالأَوَّلِ مِنَ القديمِ ، فليس فعلاً للهِ تعالى ، فلا يكون معجزةً ، ودخل فيه الفعل الذي تعلقت القدرة الحادثة بهِ ؛ كتلاوة النبيِّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ القرآنَ ، فهو معجزةٌ لرسولِ اللهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ دونَ غيرِهِ ؛ إِذْ غيرُهُ إذا تلاه إنَّما يحكيهِ ، وليس هو الآخذَ لَهُ عنِ المَلَكِ . ودخلَ ما لا تتعلَّقُ بهِ القدرة الحادثة ؛ كإحياء الموتى ، وتكثيرِ الطعام ، وانقيادِ الشجرِ ، ونحو ذلك ، وعَيَّنَ بعضُ أصحابنا في المعجزة : أن تكونَ مِنَ النوع الثاني لا الأَوَّلِ فتكون معجزة القرآن على هذا في نظمه المخصوص ، وإطلاع النبيِّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ على ذلك دون سائر الناس ، وكلا الأمرين ليسَ مِنْ فعله ولا كسبه ، وهذا الثاني أظهرُ ، والله تعالى أعلم .

فإن قلت : قد يتحدَّى النبيُّ بعدم الفعل ، كما قال عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلام : ( قَدْ عَصَمَنِي رَبِّي ) ، وكما قال نوح عليه السلامُ : ﴿ ثُمَّ أَقْضُواْ إِلَى وَلَا تُنظِرُونِ﴾ [يونس : ٧١] ، فقد وقع التحدي بعدم وقوع الفعل كالضرب والقتل . فالجواب : أَنَّ علمَهُ وإخبارَهُ بذلكَ على وَفْقِ ما ظهرَ . المعجزةُ ، وهو فعل الله خلقَهُ لهُ ، ومنهم مَنْ قَبِلَ هذا [؟] هو الاعتراض، فزادَ لإدخالِ ما ورد بعد قوله في شروط المعجزة : ( وهو فعل الله تعالى ( فقال : ( أو ما يقومُ مَقامَهُ ) . واحترزَ بقولِهِ : ( خارق للعادة ) مِنَ المعتادِ ؛ فَإِنَّهُ يستوي فيه الصادقُ والكاذبُ ، ومِنَ المعتادِ : السحر ونحوه ، وإنْ كانَ سببُهُ العادي نادراً ، خلافاً لمَنْ جعل السحر خارقاً لكن بسببٍ خاص بهِ ، ومِنَ المعتادِ أيضاً : ما يُوجَدُ في بعض الأجسامِ مِنَ الخواص ؛ كجذب الحديدِ بحجر المغناطيس
And He—glorified is He—favored by supporting them with the miracle indicating their truthfulness; and it is an act of Allah—glorified is He—, breaking the norm, accompanying the claim of prophethood, challenged by it before its occurrence, not disconfirming, rendering incapable whoever seeks to oppose it from producing its like. He guarded by the first [term] against the eternal (al-qadīm), for it is not an act of Allah—exalted is He—, so it would not be a miracle. And included in it is the act to which originated power (al-qudra al-ḥāditha) is attached, such as the recitation of the Prophet—Allah bless him and give him peace—of the Qur'an, for it is a miracle for the Messenger of Allah—Allah bless him and give him peace—to the exclusion of others; for when others recite it, they only imitate it, and they are not the ones receiving it from the angel. And included is what originated power is not attached to, such as reviving the dead, multiplying food, the bending of trees, and the like. And some of our companions specified regarding the miracle that it be of the second type, not the first, so that the miracle of the Qur'an on this view is in its particular composition, and the Prophet's—Allah bless him and give him peace—being informed of that to the exclusion of other people. And both matters are not from his act nor his acquisition, and this second [view] is more apparent, and Allah—exalted is He—knows best. For if you say: The prophet may challenge by non-action, as he—peace and blessings be upon him—said: 'My Lord has protected me,' and as Noah—peace be upon him—said: 'Then carry out your affair and do not give me respite' (Qur'an 10:71), for the challenge occurred by the non-occurrence of an act such as striking and killing. The answer: That his knowledge and his informing of that in accordance with what appeared—the miracle—is an act of Allah, He created it for him. And among them is one who accepted this objection, so he added to include what was reported after his saying in the conditions of the miracle: 'And it is an act of Allah—exalted is He—' and he said: 'Or what stands in its place.' And he guarded by his saying: 'breaking the norm' against the customary (al-muʿtād); for the truthful and the liar are equal in it. And among the customary is sorcery and the like, even if its customary cause is rare, contrary to those who consider sorcery as breaking the norm but due to a special cause. And also among the customary is what is found in some bodies of properties, such as the attraction of iron by a magnet.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a detailed definition and explanation of the miracle (muʿjiza). The author first states that Allah supports prophets with miracles that prove their truthfulness. He then gives a precise definition: a miracle is an act of Allah, breaking the norm (khāriq li-l-ʿāda), accompanying the claim of prophethood, challenged by it before its occurrence, not disconfirming, and rendering opponents incapable of producing its like. The author then explains each condition. The first condition ('act of Allah') excludes the eternal (al-qadīm) from being a miracle. It includes acts involving originated power (e.g., the Prophet's recitation of the Qur'an, which is a miracle for him alone because others only imitate it) and acts not involving originated power (e.g., reviving the dead, multiplying food). Some scholars specify that miracles must be of the second type (not involving originated power), so the Qur'an's miracle is in its composition and the Prophet's knowledge of it. After this, the author addresses an objection: what about a prophet challenging by non-action, like protection from harm? The answer is that the knowledge and announcement of that protection is itself a miracle, which is an act of Allah. Some accept this objection and add 'or what stands in its place' to the definition. Next, the author explains the condition 'breaking the norm': it excludes customary events, in which the truthful and liar are equal. Customary events include sorcery (even if its cause is rare) and physical properties like magnetism. Thus, miracles are distinguished from ordinary occurrences and from magic.

Key Terms
معجزة
قديم
قدرة حادثة
كسب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are extraordinary acts performed by the prophet using his own power.
Correction: Miracles are acts of Allah, not human acts. Even the prophet's recitation is a miracle only because Allah created it as such.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is excluded by the first condition 'act of Allah'?
A) Acts that involve originated power.
B) The eternal (al-qadīm).
C) The prophet's recitation.
D) Reviving the dead.

Key Takeaway
The first condition establishes that miracles are exclusively divine acts, not human productions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you feel the weight that it is a divine miracle revealed directly to the Prophet, or do you treat it as an ordinary book? How can you today remind yourself that every verse you recite is a challenge from Allah, proving His truth?
?
The passage emphasizes that the Prophet's recitation is a miracle only for him because he received it from the angel. Are you content to be merely an imitator of the Qur'an, or do you long to receive it with the same spiritual immediacy? What would change in your relationship with the Qur'an if you truly believed it was not your own effort but a gift from Allah?
?
Consider your daily acts of worship: do you attribute them to your own ability or to Allah's support? The first condition of a miracle is that it is purely divine. In what area of your life are you relying most on your own power instead of recognizing that every good deed is a divine act? What step will you take this week to shift that reliance?

Objection: Non-Action Challenge and Its Resolution
Sanusi addresses an objection about non-action challenges.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi resolves the objection that prophets challenge by non-action, and how the definition of miracle is adjusted.

Core Idea
Even a prophet's claim of protection is a miracle through divine act.

After defining the miracle and its first condition, Sanusi addresses an important objection: what if the prophet challenges by the absence of an action, like protection from harm? He provides a careful answer and notes that some scholars even added a phrase to the definition. This lesson explains that response.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the passage that begins with 'For if you say' and notice the examples given from the Prophet and Noah. Then read the answer.
The objection is about non-action challenges.
2
Understand the reasoning
The answer says the knowledge and announcement of the protection is itself a miracle, which is an act of Allah. Reflect on how this preserves the definition.
3
Note the addition to the definition
Some scholars accepted the objection and added 'or what stands in its place' to the condition 'act of Allah'. Identify why this is necessary.
This shows the dynamic nature of theological definitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتفضَّلَ سبحانَهُ بتأييدهم بالمعجزة الدالة على صدقهم ؛ وهي فعلُ الله سبحانه ، خارق للعادة ، مُقارِنُ لدعوى الرسالة ، مُتحدّى بهِ قبل وقوعِهِ ، غيرُ مُكَذِّبِ يُعجِزُ مَنْ يبغي معارضته عن الإتيان بمثلِهِ

فاحترزَ بالأَوَّلِ مِنَ القديمِ ، فليس فعلاً للهِ تعالى ، فلا يكون معجزةً ، ودخل فيه الفعل الذي تعلقت القدرة الحادثة بهِ ؛ كتلاوة النبيِّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ القرآنَ ، فهو معجزةٌ لرسولِ اللهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ دونَ غيرِهِ ؛ إِذْ غيرُهُ إذا تلاه إنَّما يحكيهِ ، وليس هو الآخذَ لَهُ عنِ المَلَكِ . ودخلَ ما لا تتعلَّقُ بهِ القدرة الحادثة ؛ كإحياء الموتى ، وتكثيرِ الطعام ، وانقيادِ الشجرِ ، ونحو ذلك ، وعَيَّنَ بعضُ أصحابنا في المعجزة : أن تكونَ مِنَ النوع الثاني لا الأَوَّلِ فتكون معجزة القرآن على هذا في نظمه المخصوص ، وإطلاع النبيِّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ على ذلك دون سائر الناس ، وكلا الأمرين ليسَ مِنْ فعله ولا كسبه ، وهذا الثاني أظهرُ ، والله تعالى أعلم .

فإن قلت : قد يتحدَّى النبيُّ بعدم الفعل ، كما قال عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلام : ( قَدْ عَصَمَنِي رَبِّي ) ، وكما قال نوح عليه السلامُ : ﴿ ثُمَّ أَقْضُواْ إِلَى وَلَا تُنظِرُونِ﴾ [يونس : ٧١] ، فقد وقع التحدي بعدم وقوع الفعل كالضرب والقتل . فالجواب : أَنَّ علمَهُ وإخبارَهُ بذلكَ على وَفْقِ ما ظهرَ . المعجزةُ ، وهو فعل الله خلقَهُ لهُ ، ومنهم مَنْ قَبِلَ هذا [؟] هو الاعتراض، فزادَ لإدخالِ ما ورد بعد قوله في شروط المعجزة : ( وهو فعل الله تعالى ( فقال : ( أو ما يقومُ مَقامَهُ ) . واحترزَ بقولِهِ : ( خارق للعادة ) مِنَ المعتادِ ؛ فَإِنَّهُ يستوي فيه الصادقُ والكاذبُ ، ومِنَ المعتادِ : السحر ونحوه ، وإنْ كانَ سببُهُ العادي نادراً ، خلافاً لمَنْ جعل السحر خارقاً لكن بسببٍ خاص بهِ ، ومِنَ المعتادِ أيضاً : ما يُوجَدُ في بعض الأجسامِ مِنَ الخواص ؛ كجذب الحديدِ بحجر المغناطيس
And He—glorified is He—favored by supporting them with the miracle indicating their truthfulness; and it is an act of Allah—glorified is He—, breaking the norm, accompanying the claim of prophethood, challenged by it before its occurrence, not disconfirming, rendering incapable whoever seeks to oppose it from producing its like. He guarded by the first [term] against the eternal (al-qadīm), for it is not an act of Allah—exalted is He—, so it would not be a miracle. And included in it is the act to which originated power (al-qudra al-ḥāditha) is attached, such as the recitation of the Prophet—Allah bless him and give him peace—of the Qur'an, for it is a miracle for the Messenger of Allah—Allah bless him and give him peace—to the exclusion of others; for when others recite it, they only imitate it, and they are not the ones receiving it from the angel. And included is what originated power is not attached to, such as reviving the dead, multiplying food, the bending of trees, and the like. And some of our companions specified regarding the miracle that it be of the second type, not the first, so that the miracle of the Qur'an on this view is in its particular composition, and the Prophet's—Allah bless him and give him peace—being informed of that to the exclusion of other people. And both matters are not from his act nor his acquisition, and this second [view] is more apparent, and Allah—exalted is He—knows best. For if you say: The prophet may challenge by non-action, as he—peace and blessings be upon him—said: 'My Lord has protected me,' and as Noah—peace be upon him—said: 'Then carry out your affair and do not give me respite' (Qur'an 10:71), for the challenge occurred by the non-occurrence of an act such as striking and killing. The answer: That his knowledge and his informing of that in accordance with what appeared—the miracle—is an act of Allah, He created it for him. And among them is one who accepted this objection, so he added to include what was reported after his saying in the conditions of the miracle: 'And it is an act of Allah—exalted is He—' and he said: 'Or what stands in its place.' And he guarded by his saying: 'breaking the norm' against the customary (al-muʿtād); for the truthful and the liar are equal in it. And among the customary is sorcery and the like, even if its customary cause is rare, contrary to those who consider sorcery as breaking the norm but due to a special cause. And also among the customary is what is found in some bodies of properties, such as the attraction of iron by a magnet.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a detailed definition and explanation of the miracle (muʿjiza). The author first states that Allah supports prophets with miracles that prove their truthfulness. He then gives a precise definition: a miracle is an act of Allah, breaking the norm (khāriq li-l-ʿāda), accompanying the claim of prophethood, challenged by it before its occurrence, not disconfirming, and rendering opponents incapable of producing its like. The author then explains each condition. The first condition ('act of Allah') excludes the eternal (al-qadīm) from being a miracle. It includes acts involving originated power (e.g., the Prophet's recitation of the Qur'an, which is a miracle for him alone because others only imitate it) and acts not involving originated power (e.g., reviving the dead, multiplying food). Some scholars specify that miracles must be of the second type (not involving originated power), so the Qur'an's miracle is in its composition and the Prophet's knowledge of it. After this, the author addresses an objection: what about a prophet challenging by non-action, like protection from harm? The answer is that the knowledge and announcement of that protection is itself a miracle, which is an act of Allah. Some accept this objection and add 'or what stands in its place' to the definition. Next, the author explains the condition 'breaking the norm': it excludes customary events, in which the truthful and liar are equal. Customary events include sorcery (even if its cause is rare) and physical properties like magnetism. Thus, miracles are distinguished from ordinary occurrences and from magic.

Key Terms
تحدٍ
عصمة
معجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did some scholars add to the definition of miracle to account for non-action challenges?
A) 'Or what stands in its place'
B) 'And it is breaking the norm'
C) 'And it is accompanied by a claim'
D) 'And it is preceded by a challenge'

Key Takeaway
Even a prophet's claim of protection is a miracle because the knowledge of it is a divine act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you been in a situation where you claimed Allah's protection without any visible action? How does this lesson challenge you to see that claim as a miracle from Allah, and what does that mean for your certainty in His care?
?
Do you find it easy to trust in Allah's invisible acts, or do you demand tangible evidence? Let this passage force you to examine: is your faith resting on what you can see, or on the knowledge that even your trust itself is a gift from Him?
?
If the prophet's own knowledge of protection was a miracle created by Allah, what do you make of your own moments of peace and certainty? Are you willing to recognize them as divine interventions, or do you attribute them to your own strength? Will you start thanking Allah for such 'invisible miracles' today?

Miracles

Breaking the Norm: Distinction from Magic and Natural Properties
Sanusi explains the condition of breaking the norm and what it excludes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the condition 'breaking the norm' excludes customary events, including sorcery and natural properties like magnetism.

Core Idea
Miracles are unique; magic and natural phenomena are merely rare customs.

After covering the non-action objection, Sanusi explains the second condition of a miracle: that it breaks the norm (khāriq li-l-ʿāda). This condition distinguishes miracles from ordinary events and from seemingly extraordinary occurrences like sorcery and magnetic attraction. In this lesson, we examine what is excluded by this condition.

Guided Path
1
Read the explanation of 'breaking the norm'
Read the passage starting with 'And he guarded by his saying: breaking the norm'. Understand what Sanusi excludes from miracles.
'Customary' includes sorcery and natural properties.
2
Compare sorcery and miracles
Note that sorcery, even if rare, is still considered customary because its cause is natural (even if rare). Miracles have no natural cause.
3
Reflect on examples
Think about the magnet example: it attracts iron due to a property, not a miracle. This helps clarify the boundary.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sorcery and miracles are the same because both break the norm.
Correction: Sorcery is considered customary in kalam because it has a natural cause, even if rare; miracles have no natural cause.

A) Because it is performed by magicians.
B) Because it is still considered customary.
C) Because it does not accompany a claim of prophethood.
D) Because it is an act of Allah.

Key Takeaway
Miracles must be beyond any natural cause; sorcery and magnetism are mere unusual customs.

Miracles Guarantee Prophetic Truthfulness
Sanusi argues that miracles provide necessary knowledge of truth and are never given to liars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a miracle necessarily implies the truthfulness of the prophet and cannot be performed by a liar.

Core Idea
A miracle produces certain knowledge of a prophet's truthfulness, making it impossible for a liar to perform one.

Sanusi explains that miracles are not arbitrary signs but carry a reliable, customary evidence. When God sends a miracle through a claimant to prophethood, it generates necessary knowledge (certainty) that he is truthful. This means that a liar could never be given a true miracle, because that would contradict the very certainty it produces.

Guided Path
1
Read the first part of the passage
Read from the beginning up to 'فللَّهِ الحمد على معاملته في ذلك ونحوه بمخضِ الفضل والكرم.' Notice how Sanusi establishes the customary nature of miracle evidence.
This part focuses on the main argument.
2
Understand 'necessary knowledge'
Reflect on the concept of 'al-‘ilm al-ḍarūrī' (necessary knowledge). Sanusi argues that the miracle produces such certainty that the opposite would be ignorance.
This is a key epistemological claim.
3
Observe God's consistent custom
Consider Sanusi's statement that God has always prevented liars from performing miracles and exposes false claimants quickly. This reinforces the argument.
This is an empirical observation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأَمَّا إِنْ قلنا : إنَّ دلالة المعجزة عادية بحسَب القرائن .. فحيثُ حصل العلم الضروري عنها بصدقِ الآتي بها فإنَّهُ يستحيلُ أنْ يكونَ كاذباً، وإلا انقلب العلم الضروري جهلاً، ولم يُجْرِ سبحانه وتعالى عادتَهُ مِنْ أَوَّلِ الدنيا إلى الآنَ إلا بعدم تمكين الكاذب مِنَ المعجزاتِ. وإذا خيَّل بسحرٍ ونحوِهِ أظهرَ اللهُ فضيحتَهُ عن قُرْبٍ، فللَّهِ الحمد على معاملته في ذلك ونحوه بمخضِ الفضل والكرم. ويجوز أن تظهر المعجزة على يد الكاذب لو انخرقَتِ العادةُ، ولا يحصل حينئذ بها علمُ صدقِهِ، وإلا كانَ الجهلُ علماً، وتجويز خرْقِ العادةِ عند حصولِ العلمِ بالصدق في حقِّ المحقِّ لا يقدح في العلم؛ إذ لا يلزمُ مِنْ جواز الشيء وقوعه، ألا ترى أَنَّا نُجوِّزُ استمرار عدم العالم معَ علمنا ضرورةً بوجودِهِ؛ إذْ معنى الجواز : أَنَّهُ لو قُدِّرَ واقعاً لم يلزم منه محال لذاته؛ لأنه محتمل الوقوع
As for if we say: The evidential value of the miracle is customary according to the circumstances... Then when necessary knowledge is obtained from it of the truthfulness of the one who brings it, it is impossible that he be a liar; otherwise the necessary knowledge would turn into ignorance. And He, exalted, has not conducted His custom from the beginning of the world until now except by not enabling a liar with miracles. And if he [a false prophet] produces illusions by sorcery and the like, God exposes his disgrace quickly, so praise be to God for His treatment in that and similar matters with pure grace and generosity. And it is possible for a miracle to appear at the hand of a liar if the custom were broken, but then no knowledge of his truthfulness would be obtained; otherwise ignorance would be knowledge. And the permissibility of breaking the custom at the time of obtaining knowledge of truthfulness in the case of the truthful one does not undermine knowledge, because the permissibility of a thing does not entail its actual occurrence. Do you not see that we permit the continuation of the non-existence of the world while we know necessarily its existence? For the meaning of permissibility is: if it were supposed to occur, no impossibility would follow from it in itself, because it is possible of occurrence.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage discusses miracles and their guarantee of prophetic truthfulness. It starts by stating the theory that the evidence of a miracle is customary based on circumstances; it produces necessary knowledge (certainty) of the prophet's truthfulness. Therefore, a person with such a miracle cannot be a liar, because that would convert necessary knowledge into ignorance. God's custom has always been that liars are not given miracles. If a false claimant performs sorcery, God quickly exposes him. Then the passage addresses a subtlety: it is possible in principle for a miracle to appear on a liar if God breaks the custom, but in that case, no knowledge of truth would be obtained; otherwise ignorance would be knowledge. The permissibility of custom-breaking does not undermine actual knowledge because possibility does not entail actuality. An example: we know the world exists necessarily, but we admit it is possible for it not to exist (i.e., it is contingent). The meaning of possibility is that if it were actual, no impossibility in itself would follow.

Key Terms
المعجزة
العلم الضروري
الصدق
الكاذب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are merely strong indicators but not certain proof of prophethood.
Correction: Sanusi asserts that miracles produce necessary (certain) knowledge, so they are absolute proof.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what does a miracle produce in the observer?
A) Probable belief
B) Necessary knowledge
C) Opinion
D) Doubt

Key Takeaway
A true miracle guarantees the prophet's truthfulness and cannot be performed by a liar, as it would contradict the necessary knowledge it produces.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If a miracle gives you necessary knowledge of a prophet's truthfulness, what does that say about your level of certainty in the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him)? Are you truly certain, or do you allow room for doubt that contradicts the nature of miracles?
?
God's custom is to never let a liar perform a miracle. When you hear claims of supernatural events today, do you examine them with the same standard? What would it take for you to accept a modern claim as a true miracle?
?
Sanusi says that if a miracle didn't guarantee truthfulness, necessary knowledge would become ignorance. Is there a risk in your own life of turning the clear signs of God into 'ignorance' by rationalizing or dismissing them? What would it cost you to fully embrace the certainty that miracles demand?

Miracles

The Possibility of Miracles on Liars and Custom-Breaking
Sanusi discusses the possibility of miracles on liars and the nature of logical possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that while it is theoretically possible for a miracle to appear on a liar if God breaks His custom, this does not produce knowledge of truth and does not undermine the certainty of real miracles.

Core Idea
Possibility of custom-breaking does not undermine actual knowledge of a prophet's truthfulness.

Sanusi addresses a subtle objection: if God can break His custom, could a liar perform a miracle? He admits it is logically possible, but explains that in that case no knowledge would be obtained. The mere possibility of an exception does not weaken the certainty we have from actual miracles, just as we know the world exists despite its contingency.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Read from 'ويجوز أن تظهر المعجزة على يد الكاذب' to the end. Understand the hypothetical scenario and its implications.
This part addresses a potential objection.
2
Distinguish actuality from possibility
Sanusi argues that the permissibility (jawāz) of custom-breaking does not mean it actually occurs. Actual knowledge remains intact.
This is a key logical distinction.
3
Apply the example of the world
Consider Sanusi's example: we know the world exists necessarily (by observation), but we admit it is possible for it not to exist (contingency). Similarly, we know a prophet is truthful, even though it is possible for a liar to perform a miracle in a broken custom scenario.
This clarifies the point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأَمَّا إِنْ قلنا : إنَّ دلالة المعجزة عادية بحسَب القرائن .. فحيثُ حصل العلم الضروري عنها بصدقِ الآتي بها فإنَّهُ يستحيلُ أنْ يكونَ كاذباً، وإلا انقلب العلم الضروري جهلاً، ولم يُجْرِ سبحانه وتعالى عادتَهُ مِنْ أَوَّلِ الدنيا إلى الآنَ إلا بعدم تمكين الكاذب مِنَ المعجزاتِ. وإذا خيَّل بسحرٍ ونحوِهِ أظهرَ اللهُ فضيحتَهُ عن قُرْبٍ، فللَّهِ الحمد على معاملته في ذلك ونحوه بمخضِ الفضل والكرم. ويجوز أن تظهر المعجزة على يد الكاذب لو انخرقَتِ العادةُ، ولا يحصل حينئذ بها علمُ صدقِهِ، وإلا كانَ الجهلُ علماً، وتجويز خرْقِ العادةِ عند حصولِ العلمِ بالصدق في حقِّ المحقِّ لا يقدح في العلم؛ إذ لا يلزمُ مِنْ جواز الشيء وقوعه، ألا ترى أَنَّا نُجوِّزُ استمرار عدم العالم معَ علمنا ضرورةً بوجودِهِ؛ إذْ معنى الجواز : أَنَّهُ لو قُدِّرَ واقعاً لم يلزم منه محال لذاته؛ لأنه محتمل الوقوع
As for if we say: The evidential value of the miracle is customary according to the circumstances... Then when necessary knowledge is obtained from it of the truthfulness of the one who brings it, it is impossible that he be a liar; otherwise the necessary knowledge would turn into ignorance. And He, exalted, has not conducted His custom from the beginning of the world until now except by not enabling a liar with miracles. And if he [a false prophet] produces illusions by sorcery and the like, God exposes his disgrace quickly, so praise be to God for His treatment in that and similar matters with pure grace and generosity. And it is possible for a miracle to appear at the hand of a liar if the custom were broken, but then no knowledge of his truthfulness would be obtained; otherwise ignorance would be knowledge. And the permissibility of breaking the custom at the time of obtaining knowledge of truthfulness in the case of the truthful one does not undermine knowledge, because the permissibility of a thing does not entail its actual occurrence. Do you not see that we permit the continuation of the non-existence of the world while we know necessarily its existence? For the meaning of permissibility is: if it were supposed to occur, no impossibility would follow from it in itself, because it is possible of occurrence.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage discusses miracles and their guarantee of prophetic truthfulness. It starts by stating the theory that the evidence of a miracle is customary based on circumstances; it produces necessary knowledge (certainty) of the prophet's truthfulness. Therefore, a person with such a miracle cannot be a liar, because that would convert necessary knowledge into ignorance. God's custom has always been that liars are not given miracles. If a false claimant performs sorcery, God quickly exposes him. Then the passage addresses a subtlety: it is possible in principle for a miracle to appear on a liar if God breaks the custom, but in that case, no knowledge of truth would be obtained; otherwise ignorance would be knowledge. The permissibility of custom-breaking does not undermine actual knowledge because possibility does not entail actuality. An example: we know the world exists necessarily, but we admit it is possible for it not to exist (i.e., it is contingent). The meaning of possibility is that if it were actual, no impossibility in itself would follow.

Key Terms
الخرق
العادة
الجواز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If a liar could theoretically perform a miracle, then no miracle can be trusted as proof of prophethood.
Correction: Sanusi shows that possibility does not equal actuality; actual miracles still produce certain knowledge.

Checkpoint
What does Sanusi say about the possibility of a miracle appearing on a liar?
A) It never happens under any circumstance
B) It would produce knowledge of truth
C) It is possible if custom is broken, but no knowledge results
D) It disproves the value of miracles

Key Takeaway
The theoretical possibility of a liar performing a miracle does not affect the certain knowledge we gain from actual miracles, because possibility is not actuality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about miracles, do you ever entertain doubts because they seem 'possible' to explain away? How does Sanusi's distinction between possibility and actuality challenge that doubt? Will you commit to treating the miracles of the Prophet ﷺ as certain knowledge, not mere possibilities?
?
You know with certainty that the Qur'an is a miracle. But do you live as if it is a possibility or a certainty? What would change in your daily life if you truly acted on that certainty?
?
The possibility of custom-breaking does not undermine knowledge. But have you ever allowed hypothetical possibilities to weaken your certainty in Allah's promise or punishment? For example, thinking 'maybe I won't be held accountable' as a possibility. How can this lesson help you guard against that?

Why the Arabs Failed: Inability or Sarfah?
Sanusi enumerates two explanations for Arab failure to imitate the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two explanations for the Arabs' failure to produce something like the Quran—inability and divine prevention—and why inability is the stronger view.

Core Idea
The Quran's inimitability proves its divine origin, whether through human incapacity or divine intervention.

Sanusi presents the Quran's challenge to the Arabs, masters of eloquence, who were silenced by its divine nature. He then introduces two explanations for their failure: their inherent inability (the correct view) or God's prevention (ṣarfah). This passage also gives the example of Musaylimah to illustrate the futility of imitation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
Read the passage and translation. Note that Sanusi begins by describing the Arabs' eloquence, then their silence.
The Arabs were renowned for their poetry and rhetoric.
2
Identify the two opinions
Find where he mentions the two explanations: inability and ṣarfah. Understand each.
Inability means they could not; ṣarfah means God prevented them.
3
Analyze the evidence
Look at the example of Musaylimah. How does it support the inability argument?
His attempt was laughable, showing the Quran's incomparability.
4
Reflect on the doctrinal point
Why does Sanusi prefer the inability explanation? How does this strengthen the miracle?
If they were capable but prevented, the miracle is weaker.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عارض يقدح في مناصبهم وإن كان في ذلك حتفُ أنفسهم ، فكيف بما هو مِنْ نوع البلاغة التي هي كلامهم وتَدِبُّ فيهم دبيباً ، حتى إنَّهم بها في كل وادٍ يهيمون ؟! لكن القوم أخرسهم أنَّهم أحدُّوا أنَّ الأمر إلهي لا تمكنُ مقاومتُهُ ؛ إما لأنَّهُ ليسَ في طوقهم وهو الأصح ، أو للصَّرْفة ، وهما قولان ومَنْ لم يستخي منهم ، وانْتَدَبَ لمقاومة هذا الأمر الإلهيّ ؛ كمُسَيْلِمَةَ . . افْتَضَحَ ، وأتى بمَخرَقةٍ يُتضاحَكُ منها إلى قيام الساعة
An opponent who disparages their positions even if in that is their death, so how about what is of the type of eloquence which is their speech and flows through them like a creeping, such that they wander in every valley with it? But the people were silenced because they declared that the matter is divine and cannot be resisted: either because it is beyond their ability, which is the more correct view, or because of divine prevention (al-ṣarfah), and these are two opinions. And whoever among them did not feel shy and undertook to resist this divine command, like Musaylimah... he was exposed and produced a nonsense that is laughed at until the Day of Resurrection.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage presents the challenge of the Quran's inimitability. Sanusi first describes the Arabs as masters of eloquence, yet they were unable to produce anything like the Quran. He then explains that they were silenced because they recognized the Quran as a divine command that cannot be resisted. This leads to two explanations: either they were inherently incapable (al-aṣaḥḥ, the correct view) or God prevented them (al-ṣarfah). Both prove the Quran's divine origin. As evidence of inability, he mentions Musaylimah, who attempted to imitate it and only produced laughable nonsense.

Key Terms
الإعجاز
الصرفة
مقاومة الأمر الإلهي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think al-ṣarfah implies the Arabs could have produced something like the Quran if not prevented.
Correction: Sanusi states that the correct view is that they were inherently incapable, not just prevented.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what are the two opinions on why the Arabs failed to produce something like the Quran?
A) Inability and forgetfulness
B) Inability and divine prevention (ṣarfah)
C) Disinterest and lack of motivation
D) Lack of knowledge of Arabic

Key Takeaway
The Quran's inimitability is demonstrated by the Arabs' inability—either inherent or by divine prevention—with inability being the authentic view.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that the Arabs, masters of eloquence, were silenced by the Quran's divine nature. When was the last time a verse of the Quran silenced you—stopped you in your tracks and made you realize you were standing before the speech of Allah? If it has been a while, ask yourself: Is your heart still alive to the Quran? Will you pledge today to read the Quran with the expectation that it has the power to overwhelm you?
?
Sanusi presents two opinions: the Arabs were inherently incapable of imitating the Quran, or Allah prevented them. Which of these views makes you feel more awe of the Quran? And which makes you feel more accountability—knowing that you too are incapable of producing anything like it, yet you are commanded to follow it? Has this realization changed the way you will recite the Quran tonight?
?
Musaylimah's attempt to imitate the Quran became a laughingstock. Have you ever tried to 'compete' with the Quran by prioritizing your own words or thoughts over its commands? Have you ever felt that your own desires could resist its authority? This lesson reminds you that resisting the divine command leads only to exposure and humiliation. What concrete step will you take this week to ensure that the Quran has the final say in every area of your life?

The Widespread Transmission of the Quran as Proof
Sanusi argues the Quran's widespread transmission eliminates doubt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quran's continuous widespread transmission across all groups proves its divine origin beyond doubt.

Core Idea
The Quran's universal transmission makes its divine origin unmistakable.

Sanusi presents a powerful argument based on the Quran's transmission history. He contrasts it with ordinary speech that could be doubted if only transmitted through single chains. This passage shows that the Quran's arrival to us is so pervasive and continuous that no rational person can deny it comes from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the contrast Sanusi draws between hypothetical single-narration and actual widespread transmission.
Pay attention to the rhetorical question at the end.
2
Identify the two scenarios
Sanusi presents a conditional scenario (if transmitted by single narrations) and then the reality (widespread). Locate each part in the text.
3
Understand the comprehensiveness
Note the detailed list: plains, deserts, settled areas, land, sea, believer, disbeliever, jinn, humans. This shows the transmission reached all groups.
Sanusi uses this to show no one can claim ignorance.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The rhetorical question forces the reader to acknowledge that doubt is unreasonable after such widespread transmission.
This is the core of the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أنَّهم نُقِلَ إليهمُ القرآنُ نقل غيرِهِ مِنَ الكلام نقل آحاد .. لأَمْكن الاعتذارُ عنهم بعدم الوصول ، كلا بل امتلاتْ بحَمَلَتِهِ وصُحُفِهِ وإشادة أمرِهِ الأَرضُ كلها ؛ سهلها بدوها وحضرها ، برها وبحرها، مؤمنُها وكافرها ، جِنُّها وإنسُها ، وتطاولتْ أزمنته على تلك الصفة قريباً مِنْ تسع مئة سنةٍ ، أفيستريب عاقل بعد هذا في كونهِ مِنْ  ِعندِ اللهِ جَلَّ وعلا صدَّقَ بِهِ نبيَّه صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ [وجبلها؟] وسلَّمَ ؟!
And if the Quran had been conveyed to them by single narrations as other speech is conveyed, then an excuse could have been made for them on the basis of non-receipt. But no! Rather, the whole earth was filled with its carriers, its pages, and the fame of its matter: its plains, its deserts, its settled areas, its land and sea, its believer and disbeliever, its jinn and humans. And its times extended in that condition for nearly nine hundred years. Could any intelligent person have doubt after this that it is from God, may He be glorified and exalted, which He confirmed His Prophet, may God bless him [and grant him?] peace?!
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage argues that the Quran's transmission is so widespread and continuous that it precludes any doubt. Sanusi starts by saying that if the Quran had been transmitted only by single chains (āḥād), then one could excuse the Arabs for not having received it. But in reality, the whole earth was filled with its reciters and written copies, across all regions, including plains, deserts, cities, land, sea, believers, disbelievers, jinn, and humans. Moreover, this state persisted for nearly nine hundred years. Therefore, any intelligent person cannot doubt that it is from God and that it confirms His Prophet's truthfulness.

Key Terms
تواتر
نقل آحاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Quran's transmission is comparable to ordinary human speech transmitted through single chains.
Correction: Sanusi argues that the Quran's transmission is so widespread and continuous across all groups that it cannot be doubted, unlike ordinary speech which could be questioned if from single narrations.

Checkpoint
Why does Sanusi argue that the Quran's transmission eliminates any excuse for the Arabs?
A) Because it was transmitted by single narrations
B) Because it was transmitted only in Mecca
C) Because it was widespread across all regions for centuries
D) Because the Arabs agreed to its authenticity

Key Takeaway
The Quran's universal and continuous transmission across all regions and groups for centuries makes its divine origin undeniable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi challenges: 'Could any intelligent person have doubt?' Honestly search your heart: have you ever harbored doubt about the Quran being from Allah? If yes, what was its root? If no, how does this certainty influence your daily engagement with the Quran? What will you do today to strengthen that certainty?
?
The Quran's fame filled the whole earth, reaching believers and disbelievers, jinn and humans. You too have received it—not as a passive recipient, but as a carrier. Are you actively sharing its message with those around you? What is one concrete step you will take this week to let the Quran's fame fill your household or workplace?

Prophetic Miracles: Unseen Prophecies and the Unlettered Prophet
Sanusi lists internal miracles and the unlettered Prophet as proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran's internal miracles and the Prophet's unlettered status together prove his prophethood.

Core Idea
The unlettered Prophet producing the Quran is itself a miracle.

Sanusi now presents additional internal evidences of the Quran's divine origin, focusing on its predictions of the unseen and its comprehensive teachings. He then highlights a crucial fact: these profound knowledges came through a man who never studied. This passage invites us to see the Prophet's unlettered nature as a key part of the miracle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how Sanusi builds his argument by listing internal miracles before mentioning the Prophet's unlettered state.
The verse from Surah Ankabut is a direct scriptural support.
2
Identify the internal miracles of the Quran
The passage lists several internal miracles: prophecies of the unseen, comprehensive Sharia sciences, precise proofs, refutations of opponents, stories of the past, and profound exhortations. See if you can find each one.
3
Understand the unlettered Prophet argument
Sanusi emphasizes that all this came through an unlettered Prophet who had no prior learning. This makes it impossible for him to have produced the Quran on his own. Reflect on why this is a strong proof.
Connect to the verse: if he had been literate, doubts could arise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا معَ ما فيهِ مِنَ الإخبار قبل الوقوع بالغيوب المطابقة ، ومحاسنِ علوم الشريعة المشتملة على ما لا يَقدِرُ البشرُ على ضبطِهِ ؛ مِنَ المصالح الدنيوية والأخروية ، وتحرير الأدلة ، والرد على المخالفين بالبراهينِ القطعية ، وسردِ قصص الماضينَ ، وتزكية النفس بمواعظ يغرقُ في أدنى بحارها جميع وعظ الواعظين . هذا كلُّه على يد نبي أُمِّي لم يلحظ قطُّ كتاباً ولا حصلَتْ له مخالطةٌ لذي علم ما يمكن بها تحصيل أدنى شيءٍ مِنْ ذلكَ ، عُلِمَ ذلكَ كلُّهُ بالضرورة ، ﴿ وَمَا كُنتَ تَتْلُواْ مِن قَبْلِهِ مِن كِتَبٍ وَلَا تَخطُهُ بِيَمِينِكَ إِذَا لَأَرْتَابَ الْمُبْطِلُونَ ) [العنكبوت : ٤٨] .
This, in addition to what is in it of informing about unseen matters before they occur, matching reality, and the beauties of the sciences of the Sharia that contain what humans cannot fully grasp: of worldly and otherworldly benefits, and the precise formulation of proofs, and refuting opponents with decisive arguments, and narrating stories of the past, and purifying the soul with exhortations in the least seas of which all the exhortations of the preachers drown. All this is at the hand of an unlettered Prophet who never glanced at any book nor did he have association with any person of knowledge by which he could have acquired the least thing of that. All that was known necessarily. And you did not recite before it any scripture, nor did you write it with your right hand; otherwise the falsifiers would have doubted. (Quran 29:48)
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage lists internal evidences of the Quran's divine origin. First, it contains accurate prophecies of unseen events. Second, it includes comprehensive sciences of Sharia covering worldly and otherworldly benefits, precise proofs, refutations of opponents with decisive arguments, stories of the past, and profound exhortations that surpass all human preaching. Third, all this came through an unlettered Prophet (nabī ummī) who never studied a book nor associated with scholars. This fact is known necessarily (bi-ḍarūrah). The verse from Surah Ankabut (29:48) is cited, which states that the Prophet did not read or write before the Quran, so falsifiers would have had grounds to doubt if he had.

Key Terms
أُمِّي
الغيوب
الإعجاز الداخلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Prophet could have learned from others or had secret teachers.
Correction: Sanusi emphasizes that the Prophet was unlettered and had no contact with scholars, making any human origin impossible.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's internal miracles and the Prophet's unlettered nature together provide compelling evidence of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Think of the exhortations of the Quran that 'drown' all other preaching. Which part of your soul is still untouched by its call? What would it take for you to let the Quran purify your heart as it did for the companions?
